Topic: Surgery
Question: Obstructive sleep apnoea caused by the following
Choices:
  A: Mandibular ameloblasma
  B: Dentigerous cyst
  C: Orbital fracture
  D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis
Response 0:
Thought:
  Obstructive sleep apnoea is a condition where breathing repeatedly stops and starts during sleep.
  It is caused by a blockage of the airway, usually when the soft tissue in the back of the throat collapses during sleep.
  Mandibular ameloblastoma and dentigerous cyst are benign tumors that grow in the jawbone and may cause swelling and pain, but they do not cause airway obstruction.
  Orbital fracture is a break in the bones surrounding the eye and does not cause airway obstruction.
  Bilateral TMJ ankylosis is a condition where the jaw joint is fused and cannot move properly, which may cause difficulty in opening the mouth, but it does not cause airway obstruction.
  Therefore, none of the given options are the cause of obstructive sleep apnoea.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")

  Bilateral TMJ ankylosis is a condition where the jaw joint is fused, which can cause difficulty opening the mouth and may lead to obstructive sleep apnoea.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis.

  B: Fenofibrate alone
  C: Rosuvastatin 10 mg
  D: Atorvastatin 80 mg

  Option A is a combination of Rosuvastatin and Fenofibrate, which is the preferred treatment for this patient.
  Option B is only Fenofibrate, which is not the preferred treatment for this patient.
  Option C is only Rosuvastatin, which is not the preferred treatment for this patient.
  Option D is Atorvastatin, which is a statin but does not address the high triglycerides and low HDL levels.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate.

Topic: Microbiology
Question: For which of the following is PPV-23 is most beneficial:
Choices:
  A: Cystic fibrosis patient
  B: Sickle cell anemia patient
  C: Patient with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis
  D: Child less than 2 years
Response 0:
Thought:
  PPV-23 is a pneumococcal vaccine that protects against 23 different types of pneumococcal bacteria.
  Cystic fibrosis patients are at high risk of developing pneumococcal infections.
  Sickle cell anemia patients are also at high risk of developing pneumococcal infections.
  Patients with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis may have a weakened immune system and may benefit from the vaccine.
  Children less than 2 years old are at high risk of developing pneumococcal infections.
  Therefore, the patient who is most likely to benefit from PPV-23 is the one who is at high risk of developing pneumococcal infections.
  Based on the given choices, the answer is A: Cystic fibrosis patient.
Action: Answer("A")

Thought:
  PPV-23 is a pneumococcal polysaccharide vaccine that protects against 23 types of pneumococcal bacteria.
  Cystic fibrosis patients are at higher risk of developing pneumococcal infections.
  Sickle cell anemia patients are also at higher risk of developing pneumococcal infections.
  Patients with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis may benefit from PPV-23, but it is not the most beneficial group.
  Children less than 2 years old are not recommended to receive PPV-23.
  Therefore, the most beneficial group for PPV-23 is either A: Cystic fibrosis patient or B: Sickle cell anemia patient.

Question: Pulpectomy and pulp capping are more successful in

Choices:
  A: Increased odontoblastic activity in the young
  B: Increased blood supply through the wide apex
  C: Increased volume of pulp in primary teeth
  D: Lesser amount of collagen fibres in young
Response 0:

  Pulpectomy is a root canal treatment for primary teeth.
  Pulp capping is a procedure in which a medicament is placed over an exposed pulp to encourage the formation of dentin.
  Primary teeth have a wider pulp chamber and thinner dentin walls than permanent teeth.
  Therefore, the answer is likely to be related to the characteristics of primary teeth that make them more suitable for these procedures.
  Option A is possible because young teeth have more active cells that can regenerate dentin.
  Option B is not likely because the blood supply is not a major factor in the success of these procedures.
  Option C is not likely because the volume of pulp is not a major factor in the success of these procedures.
  Option D is not likely because collagen fibers are not a major factor in the success of these procedures.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Increased odontoblastic activity in the young.

  The pulp in primary teeth has a higher regenerative capacity than permanent teeth.

  Peroxidase is an enzyme that catalyzes the breakdown of hydrogen peroxide into water and oxygen.
  NADPH oxidase is an enzyme that produces reactive oxygen species as part of the immune response.
  Superoxide dismutase is an enzyme that converts superoxide radicals into hydrogen peroxide and oxygen.
  Catalase is an enzyme that breaks down hydrogen peroxide into water and oxygen.
  Out of the given choices, NADPH oxidase seems to be the most likely enzyme that releases reactive oxygen metabolite in lysosomes.
Action: Answer("B")

  Issuing a death certificate is a legal requirement before embalming a dead body.
  Therefore, embalming without issuing a death certificate is illegal.
  To find out the section under which this act is punishable, we need to refer to the Indian Penal Code (IPC).
  After checking the IPC, we find that the correct answer is B: IPC 297.
Action: Answer("B")

  B: Supporting cusps.

  Guiding cusps are the ones that guide the jaw movement.
  Supporting cusps are the ones that support the vertical load.
  Holding cusps and Balancing cusps are not related to the jaw movement.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Guiding cusps.

Question: A lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years will show
Choices:
  A: PDL fibres attached to cementum
  B: PDL fibres attached to dentin
  C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface
  D: Co adaptation to the remaining fibres
Response 0:
Thought:
  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical procedure to gain access to the root of a tooth.
  Roots denuded for 6 years means the root surface has been exposed for 6 years.
  PDL fibres attach the cementum to the alveolar bone and help to support the tooth.
  If the root surface has been exposed for 6 years, the PDL fibres may have been lost or damaged.
  Therefore, the lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years will show that PDL fibres are not attached to cementum.
  The answer is B: PDL fibres attached to dentin.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical procedure that involves the detachment of the gingival tissue from the underlying bone to expose the root surface of the tooth.
  Roots denuded for 6 years means that the root surface has been exposed for 6 years.
  The periodontal ligament (PDL) fibres attach the tooth to the surrounding bone and cementum.
  If the root surface has been denuded for 6 years, it is likely that the PDL fibres have been lost or damaged.
  Therefore, the lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years will not show PDL fibres attached to cementum or dentin.
  Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface is a common finding in teeth with long-standing periodontal disease.
  Co-adaptation to the remaining fibres is a process that occurs after periodontal surgery, where the remaining PDL fibres adapt to the new position of the tooth.
  Therefore, the most likely answer is C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface.

  The periodontal ligament (PDL) fibres attach the tooth to the surrounding bone and cementum.
  In a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years, the PDL fibres would have been lost or destroyed.
  Therefore, the answer is not A or B.
  Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface is a common finding in teeth with roots denuded for a long time.
  Co adaptation to the remaining fibres is a process that occurs when the tooth is moved orthodontically.
  Therefore, the answer is C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface.
Action: Answer("C")
Votes: B, C, D, C, A, C, A, C, C, C

Question: Which of the following has least density?
Choices:
  A: VLDL
  B: LDL
  C: HDL
  D: Chylomicrons
Response 0:
Thought:
  All of the given options are lipoproteins.
  Lipoproteins are complexes of lipids and proteins.
  The density of lipoproteins increases with increasing protein content and decreasing lipid content.
  Chylomicrons have the highest lipid content and the least protein content, so they have the least density.
  HDL has the highest protein content and the least lipid content, so it has the highest density.
  VLDL and LDL have intermediate protein and lipid content, so their densities are between those of chylomicrons and HDL.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Chylomicrons.

Question: Iron entry into enterocytes occurs which of the following?
Choices:
  A: DMT-1
  B: Ferropoin
  C: Transferrin
  D: Hepcidin
Response 0:
Thought:
  Iron entry into enterocytes is the first step in the absorption of iron from the diet.
  DMT-1 (divalent metal transporter-1) is the primary transporter responsible for the uptake of dietary iron by enterocytes.
  Ferropoin is not a known protein involved in iron absorption.
  Transferrin is a protein that transports iron in the blood, but it is not involved in iron absorption by enterocytes.
  Hepcidin is a hormone that regulates iron metabolism, but it is not involved in iron entry into enterocytes.
  Therefore, the answer is A: DMT-1.

Thought:
  Iron entry into enterocytes is the first step in iron absorption.
  DMT-1 is a transmembrane protein that mediates the transport of ferrous iron across the apical membrane of enterocytes.
  Ferropoin is not a known protein involved in iron absorption.
  Transferrin is a protein that binds to iron and transports it in the blood.
  Hepcidin is a hormone that regulates iron metabolism by controlling the amount of iron that is absorbed from the diet.
  Therefore, the protein that mediates the transport of ferrous iron across the apical membrane of enterocytes is DMT-1.

Question: A female come to gynaeoPD for preconceptual counseling, with history of two second trimester aboions. What is the next investigation you will advice
Choices:
  A: TVS
  B: hysteroscopy
  C: Endometrial biopsy
  D: chromosomal abnormalities
Response 0:
Thought:
  Preconceptual counseling is given to a woman who is planning to conceive.
  The woman has a history of two second-trimester abortions.
  Second-trimester abortions are usually due to fetal abnormalities, uterine anomalies, or cervical incompetence.
  The next investigation should be aimed at identifying the cause of the previous abortions.
  Chromosomal abnormalities can cause fetal abnormalities and miscarriages.
  Therefore, the next investigation should be chromosomal abnormalities.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Preconceptual counseling is given to women who are planning to conceive.
  The woman has a history of two second trimester abortions.
  Second trimester abortions are those that occur between 14 and 26 weeks of pregnancy.
  The most common causes of second trimester abortions are chromosomal abnormalities, uterine abnormalities, and cervical incompetence.
  Therefore, the next investigation that should be advised is to determine the cause of the previous abortions.
  Chromosomal abnormalities are the most common cause of second trimester abortions.
  Therefore, the next investigation that should be advised is chromosomal abnormalities.
  The answer is D: chromosomal abnormalities.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Preconceptual counseling is provided to women who are planning to conceive.
  The woman has a history of two second-trimester abortions.
  Second-trimester abortions can be caused by various factors, including chromosomal abnormalities, uterine anomalies, and cervical incompetence.
  The next investigation should aim to identify the cause of the previous abortions.
  Transvaginal ultrasound (TVS) can help identify uterine anomalies and cervical incompetence.
  Hysteroscopy can also identify uterine anomalies and evaluate the endometrial cavity.
  Endometrial biopsy can help identify endometrial abnormalities.
  Chromosomal abnormalities can be identified by karyotyping.
  Based on the above, the most appropriate investigation to advise would be TVS.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 3:
Thought:
  Preconceptual counseling is provided to women who are planning to conceive.
  A history of two second trimester abortions indicates a potential problem with the pregnancy.
  The next investigation should be aimed at identifying the cause of the problem.
  TVS (transvaginal ultrasound) can be used to detect any structural abnormalities in the uterus or cervix.
  Hysteroscopy can be used to visualize the inside of the uterus and detect any abnormalities.
  Endometrial biopsy can be used to detect any abnormalities in the lining of the uterus.
  Chromosomal abnormalities can be a cause of recurrent pregnancy loss.

  The site of action of ADH is on the distal tubules and collecting ducts in the kidney.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Distal tubules and collecting ducts in the kidney.

Question: Object permanence seen in which stage of Jean Piagets theory
Choices:
  A: Sensorimotor
  B: Pre-operational stage
  C: Concrete operations stage
  D: Formal operations stage
Response 0:
Thought:
  Object permanence is the understanding that objects continue to exist even when they cannot be seen, heard, or touched.
  Jean Piaget's theory of cognitive development has four stages: Sensorimotor, Pre-operational, Concrete operations, and Formal operations.
  The Sensorimotor stage is the first stage, which occurs from birth to 2 years old.
  During the Sensorimotor stage, infants learn about the world through their senses and actions.
  Object permanence is a major achievement of the Sensorimotor stage.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Sensorimotor.

Topic: Physiology
Question: Which of the following is rapid source of energy by resynthesizing ATP for exercising muscles is?
Choices:
  A: Glycolysis
  B: Glycogenolysis
  C: TCA cycle
  D: Phosphocreatine
Response 0:
Thought:
  The question is asking for a rapid source of energy for exercising muscles.
  Glycolysis and glycogenolysis are processes that break down glucose and glycogen respectively to produce energy.
  TCA cycle is a process that produces energy from the breakdown of glucose, fatty acids, and amino acids.
  Phosphocreatine is a molecule that can donate a phosphate group to ADP to rapidly resynthesize ATP.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Phosphocreatine.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:

  The question is asking for a rapid source of energy for exercising muscles.

  The TCA cycle is a slower process that occurs in the mitochondria to produce ATP.

  Therefore, the answer is D: Phosphocreatine.

Choices:
  A: Langerhans cell histiocytosis
  B: Giant cell tumor
  C: Chondroblastoma
  D: Osteoid osteoma
Response 0:
Thought:
  The patient is a 9 year old boy with a lytic lesion on midshaft tibia.
  The HPE shows grooved nuclei, giant cells, eosinophilic cytoplasm and fibroblastic proliferation.
  The X-ray shows an eccentric lytic lesion with cortical thinning and expansion.
  Langerhans cell histiocytosis, also known as eosinophilic granuloma, is a rare condition that can cause lytic bone lesions. It is characterized by the presence of Langerhans cells, which are a type of dendritic cell.
  Giant cell tumor is a benign bone tumor that can also cause lytic lesions. It is characterized by the presence of multinucleated giant cells.
  Chondroblastoma is a rare benign bone tumor that typically occurs in the epiphysis of long bones. It is characterized by the presence of chondroblasts, which are cells that produce cartilage.
  Osteoid osteoma is a benign bone tumor that typically occurs in the cortex of long bones. It is characterized by the presence of osteoblasts, which are cells that produce bone.
  Based on the age of the patient, the location of the lesion, and the histological findings, the most likely diagnosis is A: Langerhans cell histiocytosis.

### Exam: medmcqa-dev-100 | Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 80 of 100 ###
Topic: Pharmacology
Question: Which of the following instructions should be given to a lactating mother regarding drug usage?
Choices:
  A: No advice is required as most of the drugs are secreted negligibly in the milk
  B: Take drugs with longer half-life
  C: Tell her to feed the baby just before next dose
  D: Do not feed the baby if you are consuming any drug
Response 0:
Thought:
  Lactating mothers should be cautious while taking drugs as it can affect the baby through milk.
  Most of the drugs are secreted in the milk, so advice is required.
  Longer half-life drugs will stay longer in the mother's body and will be secreted in milk for a longer time, so it is not a good option.
  Feeding the baby just before the next dose will not help as the drug will still be present in the milk.
  The best option is to avoid drugs that are not necessary or take drugs that are safe for lactating mothers.
  Therefore, none of the options are correct.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Lactating mothers should be careful while taking drugs as it can be secreted in the milk and can affect the baby.
  Most of the drugs are secreted in the milk, so advice is required.
  Taking drugs with longer half-life can increase the concentration of drugs in milk.
  Telling the mother to feed the baby just before the next dose can reduce the concentration of drugs in milk.
  Asking the mother not to feed the baby if she is consuming any drug is not a good option as it can lead to malnutrition in the baby.
  Therefore, the best option is C: Tell her to feed the baby just before the next dose.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Lactating mothers should be cautious about drug usage as some drugs can be secreted in the milk and can harm the baby.
  Most of the drugs are secreted negligibly in the milk, but some drugs can be harmful to the baby.
  Taking drugs with longer half-life can increase the amount of drug secreted in the milk.
  Telling the mother to feed the baby just before the next dose can reduce the amount of drug secreted in the milk.
  Instructing the mother to not feed the baby if she is consuming any drug can be harmful to the baby as it can lead to malnutrition.
  Therefore, the best advice would be to tell the mother to feed the baby just before the next dose.

  B: Repaglinide
  C: Vildagliptin
  D: Glimepiride
Response 0:
Thought:
  The patient has stage 5 chronic kidney disease, which means the kidneys are severely damaged and have a glomerular filtration rate (GFR) of less than 15 ml/min/1.73m.
  In such patients, the use of metformin is contraindicated due to the risk of lactic acidosis.
  The patient doesn't want to take injectable insulin.
  Among the given options, Linagliptin and Vildagliptin are DPP-4 inhibitors, and Repaglinide and Glimepiride are sulfonylureas.
  DPP-4 inhibitors are preferred over sulfonylureas in patients with renal impairment because they do not require dose adjustment.
  Therefore, the preferred oral hypoglycemic agent in this patient would be either Linagliptin or Vildagliptin.

  B: Basal cell carcinoma

  D: Leukoplakia

  Basal cell carcinoma is a type of skin cancer that grows slowly and rarely spreads to other parts of the body.

  Systematic random sampling is used when the population is large and there is a list of all the individuals in the population.

  Stratified random sampling is used when the population is heterogeneous and can be divided into subgroups.
  Cluster sampling is used when the population is large and spread out over a wide area.
  The question is asking about selecting patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results.
  Stratified random sampling is used for selecting patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results.
  Therefore, the answer is C: Stratified random sampling.
